### Post by Vaphell on 2012-11-08
what do you mean by 'resize'? trim to fit the terminal size?
you should pack your data into array and use some math to do *echo ${line[n]:$start:$end}* in a loop. In bash width and height are stored in $COLUMNS and $LINES

---

### Post by Abhinav Kumar on 2012-11-08
Hi,
I think you can use this command to change the font size 
```

#here, Monospace is the font and 11 is the font size
gconftool-2 --set /desktop/gnome/interface/monospace_font_name --type string "Monospace 11"

```Also, have a look at
[http://ubuntu-tutorials.com/2008/01/10/gconftool-2-gconf-editor-from-the-shell/](http://ubuntu-tutorials.com/2008/01/10/gconftool-2-gconf-editor-from-the-shell/)

Regards,
Abhinav

### Post by Abhinav Kumar on 2012-11-09
> **conradin said:**
> I tried the examples here:
[http://unix.stackexchange.com/questions/37260/change-font-in-echo-command](http://unix.stackexchange.com/questions/37260/change-font-in-echo-command)
but as the OP noted, the smaller function failed. 

I dont want to trim anything, and I dont want to change my terminal font for an extended period. I just want smaller text to be displayed while the script runs. When it closes, I want things back to normal. 

maybe export and source commands can do it....
At the start of the script use 
```

gconftool-2 --set /desktop/gnome/interface/monospace_font_name --type string "Monospace 5"

```

At the end of the script, use 
```

gconftool-2 --set /desktop/gnome/interface/monospace_font_name --type string "Monospace 11"

```
This will restore the font to default size

Regards,
Abhinav

### Post by Vaphell on 2012-11-15
imo you should pack frames into an array

```
#!/bin/bash

frame[0]="@@@...
...
...@@@"

frame[1]="@@@...
...
...@@@"

...

frame[25]="@@@...
...
...@@@"

while :
do
  for(( i=0; i<${#frame[@]}; i++ ))
  do
    sleep 0.2
    clear
    echo "${frame[i]}"
  done
done
```

it would be even nicer to move the gfx to external text files and load them

```
# assuming alphabetical order 00 01 02 ... 20 21 ...
for f in *.txt
do
  frame+=( "$( < $f )" )
done
```
